Distinguishing Mut'ah from Muwaqqat: Wording, Conditions, and Subsidiary Rulings
Explaining the distinctions and subsidiary rulings related to mut'ah and muwaqqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mut'ah from muwaqqat by their wording and legal effect, and apply the subsidiary rulings on conditions, intentions, and daytime marriage.

Core Idea
Mut'ah and muwaqqat differ in wording but share the same prohibition; a condition to divorce does not invalidate, but a time limit does.

While both mut'ah and muwaqqat are invalid, scholars have discussed their linguistic and structural differences. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores these distinctions and also addresses related scenarios: marrying with a condition to divorce, with an intention of separation, and the case of 'daytime marriage' (al-nahariyyat). This lesson clarifies these fine points.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types by wording
Note the difference: muwaqqat uses the words 'nikah' or 'tazwij' with a specified time and witnesses; mut'ah uses the words 'tamattu' or 'istimta''. However, the verification from Fath al-Qadir collapses them: both are mut'ah because neither aims at permanence.
The linguistic form does not change the ruling.
2
Identify the effect of a condition to divorce
If a man marries with the condition that he will divorce after a month, the marriage is valid and the condition is void. The reason: the stipulation of a terminating condition (qāṭi‘) indicates that the contract is intended to be permanent; the condition contradicts that, so it is invalid.
This is different from a time limit.
3
Understand the role of intention vs. explicit wording
If the husband merely intends to stay with the wife for a period but does not mention it in the contract, the marriage is valid. Time-binding is only effective through explicit wording, not mere intention.
The contract is judged by its terms, not hidden intentions.
4
Examine the case of daytime marriage (al-nahariyyat)
It is permissible to marry a woman with the understanding that the husband will stay with her only during the day. However, this condition is not binding on the wife; she can request nights as per the rules of division (qasm).
This is not a time-limited marriage but a conditional arrangement on cohabitation.
5
Apply the rulings to various durations
The prohibition of muwaqqat applies even to very long periods (e.g., 200 years) and to unknown durations. The key is the specification of a time, regardless of length.
The term 'muwaqqat' is absolute and covers all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبطل نكاح المتعة والموقت وفرق بينهما في النهاية والمعراج بأن يذكر في الموقت لفظ النكاح أو التزويج مع التوقيت وفي المتعة لفظ «أتمتع بك» أو «أستمتع». وفي العناية بفرق آخر أن الموقت يكون بحضرة الشهود ويذكر فيه مدة معينة بخلاف المتعة فإنه لو قال «أتمتع بك» ولم يذكر مدة كان متعة. والتحقيق ما في فتح القدير أن المتعة عقد على امرأة لا يراد به مقاصد عقد النكاح من القرار للولد وتربيته بل إما إلى مدة معينة ينتهي العقد بانتهائها أو غير معينة بمعنى بقاء العقد ما دام معها إلى أن ينصرف عنها فيدخل فيه بمادة المتعة والنكاح الموقت أيضاً فيكون من أفراد المتعة وإن عقد بلفظ التزويج وأحضر الشهود إلى آخر ما ذكره. وقد نقل في الهداية إجماع الصحابة على حرمته وأنها كانت مباحة ثم نسخت. وفي صحيح مسلم عنه كنت أذنت لكم في الاستمتاع بالنساء وقد حرم الله ذلك إلى يوم القيامة (۱) والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة شهيرة، وما نقل عن ابن عباس من إباحتها فقد صح رجوعه وما في الهداية من نسبته إلى مالك فغلط كما ذكره الشارحون، فحينئذ كان زفر القائل بإباحة الموقت محجوجاً بالإجماع لما علمت أن الموقت من أفراد المتعة. قالوا : ثلاثة أشياء نسخت مرتين : المتعة ولحوم الحمر الأهلية والتوجه إلى بيت المقدس. أطلق في الموقت فشمل المدة الطويلة أيضاً كأن يتزوجها إلى مائتي سنة وهو ظاهر المذهب وهو الصحيح كما في المعراج، لأن التأقيت هو المعين لجهة المتعة. وشمل المدة المجهولة أيضاً. وقيد بالموقت لأنه لو تزوجها على أن يطلقها بعد شهر، فإنه جائز لأن اشتراط القاطع يدل على انعقاده مؤبداً وبطل الشرط. كما في القنية. ولو تزوجها وفي نيته أن يقعد معها مدة نواها فالنكاح صحيح لأن التوقيت إنما يكون باللفظ. قالوا: ولا بأس بتزوج النهاريات وهو أن يتزوجها ليقعد معها نهاراً دون الليل. وينبغي أن لا يكون هذا الشرط لازماً عليها ولها أن تطلب المبيت عندها ليلاً لما عرف في باب القسم.
His statement: 'and the marriage of mut'ah and muwaqqat is invalid, and the difference between them in al-Nihayah and al-Mi'raj is that in muwaqqat the word 'nikah' or 'tazwij' is mentioned along with specification of a time, while in mut'ah the wording 'I enjoy you' or 'I seek enjoyment' is used. In al-Inayah there is another difference: muwaqqat occurs in the presence of witnesses and a specific time is mentioned, unlike mut'ah because if he says 'I enjoy you' without mentioning a time, it is mut'ah. The verification is in Fath al-Qadir: mut'ah is a contract with a woman which does not aim at the objectives of marriage such as establishing lineage and raising children, but either for a specific time after which the contract ends, or for an unspecified time meaning the contract continues as long as he stays with her until he leaves her. Thus, it includes what is expressed with the root of enjoyment (mut'ah) and also time-limited marriage, so muwaqqat is a subset of mut'ah, even if contracted with the word 'tazwij' and with witnesses, to the end of what he mentioned. It is reported in al-Hidayah that there is consensus of the Companions on its prohibition, and that it was initially permissible and then abrogated. In Sahih Muslim: 'I had permitted you enjoyment of women, and Allah has prohibited that until the Day of Judgment.' The hadiths on this are numerous and well-known. The report from Ibn Abbas permitting it is established that he retracted. The attribution in al-Hidayah to Malik is a mistake, as the commentators mentioned. Thus, Zafar who says muwaqqat is permissible is defeated by consensus because it is known that muwaqqat is a subset of mut'ah. They said: Three things were abrogated twice: mut'ah, the meat of domestic donkeys, and facing Jerusalem (in prayer). The ruling (in the text) is absolute regarding muwaqqat, so it includes even a long period, such as marrying a woman for two hundred years, and this is the apparent madhhab and the correct view as in al-Mi'raj, because specifying a time defines the nature of mut'ah. It also includes an unknown period. It is restricted to time-bound marriage because if he marries her with the condition that he will divorce her after a month, it is valid because the stipulation of a terminating condition indicates that the contract is permanent and the condition is void, as in al-Qunyah. If he marries her with the intention of staying with her for a period he intends, the marriage is valid because time-binding is only by explicit wording. They said: There is no harm in marrying 'daytime women', which is that he marries a woman to stay with her during the day and not at night. It should be that this condition is not binding on her, and she has the right to request spending the night with her, as is known in the section on division of nights.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that both mut'ah (temporary marriage) and muwaqqat (time-bound marriage) are invalid and prohibited. The commentator first distinguishes between them based on wording and presentation: muwaqqat uses the words 'nikah' or 'tazwij' along with a specified time and witnesses, while mut'ah uses 'tamattu' or 'istimta''. However, the verification from Fath al-Qadir is that muwaqqat is essentially a subset of mut'ah because both involve a contract that does not intend permanence or the objectives of marriage like lineage and child-rearing. The evidence for prohibition is strong: ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, the hadith in Sahih Muslim where the Prophet (pbuh) says Allah has prohibited it until the Day of Judgment, and numerous other narrations. The passage also mentions that Ibn Abbas's earlier permissive view was retracted, and an attribution to Malik in al-Hidayah is a mistake. Zafar's opinion permitting muwaqqat is refuted by consensus. Key Terms
النهاريات (al-nahariyyat): A marriage where the husband stays with the wife only during the day and not at night; considered permissible but the wife can request night stays.
القاطع (al-qāṭi‘): A terminating condition that, if stipulated, implies the contract is intended to be permanent; the condition itself is void.
التوقيت باللفظ (al-tawqīt bi’l-lafẓ): Time-binding through explicit wording; mere intention does not make a marriage muwaqqat.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a marriage hinges on the presence of a time limit in the contract wording; conditions on divorce or intention do not invalidate, and daytime marriages are permissible but not binding on the wife.

Intercourse After a Judge's Ruling on False Witnesses: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intercourse after a false marriage claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on intercourse after a judge's ruling based on false witnesses, explain his dalil, and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
The judge's ruling based on apparent evidence is binding internally to prevent endless dispute.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of a judge's ruling when the underlying witnesses are later discovered to be false. The central question: does the ruling permit the man to have intercourse with the woman, even though he did not actually marry her? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, and their arguments reveal deeper principles about the relationship between external legal rulings and inner reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the passage to identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa's permission versus the Sahibayn's prohibition. Note the exact scenario: a woman claims marriage, brings witnesses, judge rules in her favor, but the man did not actually marry her.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the judge erred because the witnesses were false. They analogize to the case where witnesses are later found to be slaves or disbelievers. Understand why this analogy is used and what it implies for the validity of the ruling.
Slaves and disbelievers are disqualified from testifying in certain cases.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: slavery and disbelief are easily verifiable at the time of judgment, whereas the inner truthfulness of witnesses is not. Therefore, the ruling must be given effect internally to avoid endless contention. Understand the principle of 'cutting off dispute' (qat' al-munaza'ah).
4
Extract the tarjih
Although the text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, the madhhab generally follows Abu Hanifa in such procedural matters. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, no hadd; under the Sahibayn, hadd may apply.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a similar case where the judge rules based on a forged document. Would the same principle apply? Test your understanding of the underlying illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وله وطء امرأة ادعت أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها ببينة ولم يكن تزوجها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ليس له وطؤها لأن القاضي أخطأ الحجة إذ الشهود كذبة فصار كما إذا ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار. ولأبي حنيفة أن الشهود صدقة عنده وهو الحجة لتعذر الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق بخلاف الكفر والرق لأن الوقوف عليهما متيسر فإذا ابتنى القضاء على الحجة وأمكن تنفيذه باطناً بتقديم النكاح نفذ قطعاً للمنازعة بخلاف الأملاك المرسلة لأن في اشتراط الشهود وتعيين المدة وفي الموقت الشهود وتعيين المدة.
His statement: 'And he may have intercourse with a woman who claimed that he married her and the judge ruled in her favor based on witnesses, even though he had not married her.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may not have intercourse with her because the judge erred in the evidence, since the witnesses were liars, so it is as if they turned out to be slaves or disbelievers. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the witnesses are truthful in his (the judge's) view, and they are the evidence because it is impossible to ascertain the inner truth of their honesty, unlike disbelief or being a slave because those are easily verifiable. So when the judgment is based on evidence and it is possible to implement it internally by considering the marriage to have taken place, it is executed definitively to stop contention, unlike general properties (claims) because in marriage there is the requirement of witnesses and specification of a time, and in muwaqqat there are witnesses and specification of a time.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a scenario where a woman falsely claims that a man married her and brings false witnesses to support her claim. The judge rules in her favor, establishing the marriage externally based on the witnesses. The question is whether the man may lawfully have intercourse with her. According to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible. His reasoning: the judge's ruling is based on the apparent evidence (the witnesses), and since the inner truth of their honesty cannot be verified (unlike obvious disqualifications like being slaves or disbelievers), the ruling must be given effect both externally and internally to prevent conflict. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that it is not permissible because the judge's ruling was based on false evidence; once the falseness is known, the ruling is void internally, just as if the witnesses were later discovered to be slaves or disbelievers. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: slavery and disbelief are easily verifiable at the time of judgment, whereas the inner truth of honesty is not. Therefore, the ruling stands. The passage ends with a comparison to general property claims, noting that marriage cases involve witnesses and time specification, unlike other claims.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): The evidence in a legal case, specifically the testimony of witnesses who establish the marriage externally.
الحجة (al-hujjah): The legal proof or evidence upon which the judge bases his ruling; here, the witnesses' testimony is considered the hujjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Hanifa reject the Sahibayn's analogy to witnesses who are slaves or disbelievers?
A) Because slaves and disbelievers can never be witnesses in marriage cases.
B) Because the dishonesty of witnesses is not easily verifiable at the time of judgment, unlike slavery or disbelief.
C) Because the Sahibayn misapplied the analogy.
D) Because Abu Hanifa holds that all witnesses are truthful until proven otherwise.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a judge's ruling based on apparent evidence is binding internally to prevent endless disputes, even if the evidence is later discovered to be false, provided the falsity was not easily verifiable at the time.

Understanding Mut'a and the Prohibition of Timed Marriage
Defines mut'a and clarifies its inclusion of timed marriage, citing consensus on prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mut'a, explain why any timed marriage is a form of mut'a and therefore haram, and cite the consensus of the Companions as proof.

Core Idea
Any marriage with a time limit, explicit or implicit, is mut'a and haram by consensus.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the true nature of mut'a (temporary marriage) and shows that it includes any marriage contract with a fixed or implied duration, even if the word 'nikah' is used. The prohibition is established by the consensus of the Companions and authentic hadith. We also examine the details: long durations, unknown durations, and the invalidity of stipulations that contradict permanence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Definition
Mut'a is a contract not intended for permanence or procreation, but for temporary enjoyment. Timed marriage (nikah muwaqqat) is included even if worded as 'nikah'.
The passage emphasizes that the essence is intent, not wording.
2
Locate the Proof
The Hidayah reports Ijma of the Companions on prohibition; Sahih Muslim quotes the Prophet's abrogation: 'I permitted you temporary enjoyment... Allah has forbidden it until the Day of Judgment.'
The hadith is decisive and well-known.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The explicit statement of abrogation and the consensus indicate definitive prohibition. The passage also shows that timed marriage is a subset of mut'a, thus covered by the same ruling.
Ijma is a qat'i dalil.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf and the Hanafi Response
Zufar held timed marriage permissible, but he is refuted by consensus. The passage notes that even Ibn Abbas retracted his earlier permission.
The author attributes the permissibility view to Zufar and rejects it.
5
Apply the Ruling to Various Scenarios
Long durations (e.g., 200 years), unknown durations, and stipulations like 'divorce after a month' are all forms of timed marriage. Intention alone does not create timing; only verbal expression matters.
Daytime marriage is permissible but the wife can claim nighttime rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والموقت وله وطء امرأة ادعت عليه أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها ببينة ولم يكن تزوجها .
معنى
بخلاف المتعة فإنه لو قال «أتمتع بك ولم يذكر مدة كان متعة. والتحقيق ما في فتح القدير أن المتعة عقد على امرأة لا يراد به مقاصد عقد النكاح من القرار للولد وتربيته بل إما إلى مدة معينة ينتهي العقد بانتهائها أو غير معينة بمعنى بقاء العقد ما دام معها إلى أن ينصرف عنها فيدخل فيه بمادة المتعة والنكاح الموقت أيضاً فيكون من أفراد المتعة وإن عقد بلفظ التزويج وأحضر الشهود إلى آخر ما ذكره. وقد نقل في الهداية إجماع الصحابة على حرمته وأنها كانت مباحة ثم نسخت. وفي صحيح مسلم عنه كنت أذنت لكم في الاستمتاع الله ذلك إلى يوم القيامة» (۱) والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة شهيرة، وما نقل عن
بالنساء وقد حرم ابن عباس من إباحتها فقد صح رجوعه وما في الهداية من نسبته إلى مالك فغلط كما ذكره الشارحون، فحينئذ كان زفر القائل بإباحة الموقت محجوجاً بالإجماع لما علمت أن الموقت من أفراد المتعة. قالوا : ثلاثة أشياء نسخت مرتين : المتعة ولحوم الحمر الأهلية والتوجه إلى بيت المقدس. أطلق في الموقت فشمل المدة الطويلة أيضاً كأن يتزوجها إلى مائتي سنة وهو ظاهر المذهب وهو الصحيح كما في المعراج، لأن التأقيت هو المعين لجهة المتعة. وشمل المدة المجهولة أيضاً. وقيد بالموقت لأنه لو تزوجها على أن يطلقها بعد شهر، فإنه جائز لأن اشتراط القاطع يدل على انعقاده مؤبداً وبطل الشرط. كما في القنية. ولو تزوجها وفي نيته أن يقعد معها مدة نواها فالنكاح صحيح لأن التوقيت إنما يكون باللفظ. قالوا: ولا بأس بتزوج النهاريات وهو أن يتزوجها ليقعد معها نهاراً دون الليل. وينبغي أن لا يكون هذا الشرط لازماً عليها ولها أن تطلب المبيت عندها ليلاً لما عرف في باب القسم. قوله: (وله وطء امرأة ادعت أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها مبينة ولم يكن تزوجها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ليس له وطؤها لأن القاضي أخطأ الحجة إذ الشهود كذبة فصار كما إذا ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار. ولأبي حنيفة أن الشهود صدقة عنده وهو الحجة لتعذر الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق بخلاف الكفر والرق لأن الوقوف عليهما متيسر فإذا ابتنى القضاء على الحجة وأمكن تنفيذه باطناً بتقديم النكاح نفذ قطعاً للمنازعة بخلاف الأملاك المرسلة لأن في
اشتراط الشهود وتعيين المدة وفي الموقت الشهود وتعيين المدة. قال في الفتح : ولا شك أنه لا دليل لهؤلاء على تعيين كون نكاح المتعة الذي أباحه ثـم حـرمـه هـو مـا اجـتـمـع فـيـه مـادة م ت ع للقطع من الآثار بأن المتحقق ليس إلا أنه أذن لهم في المتعة، وليس معنى هذا أن من باشر هذا المأذون فيه يتعين عليه أن يخاطبها بلفظ التمتع ونحوه لما عرف من أن اللفظ إنما يطلق ويراد
And the timed [marriage] - and he has the right to have intercourse with a woman who claimed that he married her and the judge ruled in favor of her marriage based on evidence while he did not marry her. Unlike mut'a, because if he said 'I enjoy being with you' and did not mention a duration, it is mut'a. The verification is what is in Fath al-Qadir: mut'a is a contract with a woman by which the purposes of the marriage contract—permanence for offspring and upbringing—are not intended; rather, it either has a specified duration after which the contract ends, or an unspecified one meaning the contract remains as long as she is with him until he departs from her. Thus, it includes what is of the root of mut'a and also the timed marriage, so it becomes a type of mut'a even if contracted with the wording of marriage and with witnesses, up to what he mentioned. And it has been narrated in al-Hidayah the consensus of the Companions on its prohibition, and that it was permissible then abrogated. And in Sahih Muslim from him: 'I permitted you temporary enjoyment... Allah [has forbidden it] until the Day of Judgment.' The hadiths on this are many and well-known. And what has been narrated from... women, and Ibn Abbas [later] forbade it, and his retraction is authenticated. And what is in al-Hidayah attributing [the view of permissibility] to Malik is an error, as the commentators mentioned. Thus, Zufar, who says the timed [marriage] is permissible, is refuted by consensus, for you know that the timed is a type of mut'a. They said: three things were abrogated twice: mut'a, the meat of domestic donkeys, and facing toward Jerusalem. He made the ruling absolute regarding the timed marriage, so it includes even a long duration, like marrying her for two hundred years—that is the apparent madhhab and it is correct as in al-Mi'raj, because the timing is what specifies the nature of mut'a. It also includes an unknown duration. It is restricted to timed marriage because if he marries her with the stipulation that he will divorce her after a month, it is valid, because the stipulation of termination indicates the contract is permanent and the stipulation is void, as in al-Qunyah. And if he marries her with the intention of staying with her for a duration but not expressed, the marriage is valid because timing is only by verbal expression. They said: There is no harm in marrying 'daytime women'—that is, he marries her to stay with her during the day but not the night. This stipulation should not be binding on her, and she has the right to request overnight stay with her at night, as is known in the section on division. His statement: 'And he has the right to have intercourse with a woman who claimed that he married her and the judge ruled in favor of her marriage with evidence while he did not marry her'—this is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not have the right to have intercourse with her because the judge made an error in the proof, since the witnesses are liars, so it is like when they appear to be slaves or disbelievers. For Abu Hanifa, the witnesses are truthful according to him, and they are the proof, because it is impossible to ascertain the reality of truthfulness, unlike disbelief and slavery because ascertaining them is easy. So when the ruling is based on proof and it is possible to execute it inwardly by assuming the marriage, it executes definitively to end the dispute, unlike absolute possessions because in... stipulation of witnesses and specifying the duration, and in timed marriage, witnesses and specifying the duration. He said in al-Fath: There is no doubt that there is no evidence for these people to specify that the mut'a marriage which was permitted then forbidden is that which combines the root m-t-' (mut'a) based on the definitive transmission that what is verified is only that he permitted them temporary enjoyment, and this does not mean that the one who engages in this permitted act must address her with the wording of 'tamattu'' or the like, because it is known that the wording is only used and intended...
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and commentary on temporary marriage (mut'a) and timed marriage (nikah muwaqqat). The author clarifies that any marriage with a fixed or implied duration is a form of mut'a, regardless of the wording used (even if the word 'nikah' is used with witnesses). He cites the consensus of the Companions on its prohibition, as transmitted by the Hidayah, that mut'a was originally permissible but then abrogated. The hadith from Sahih Muslim is quoted: Allah forbade it until the Day of Judgment. He also refutes Zufar's opinion that timed marriage is permissible, showing it is part of mut'a. The passage then discusses details: timing can be long (e.g., 200 years) or unknown; a stipulation to divorce after a month is void because it contradicts permanence. Intention alone does not create timing; only verbal expression matters. 'Daytime marriage' is permissible but the wife can demand nighttime rights. The main teaching is that any form of temporary marriage is prohibited by consensus.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'a): A temporary marriage contract intended for sexual enjoyment with a specified or unspecified duration, not for permanence or procreation.
النكاح الموقت (al-nikah al-muwaqqat): A marriage contracted with a fixed or implied time limit; considered a form of mut'a and therefore prohibited.
التوقيت (al-tawqit): The act of setting a time limit in a marriage contract, which renders the contract invalid as nikah and turns it into mut'a.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a marriage contract where the husband states, 'I marry you for one year' with witnesses and the word 'nikah'?
A) Valid permanent marriage, condition void
B) Mut'a, which is haram
C) Permissible as nikah muwaqqat
D) Void because of ignorance

Key Takeaway
Any marriage contract with a time limit is mut'a and haram by consensus of the Companions.

Nikah — Marriage

Ruling on Intercourse When a Judge Declares a Marriage Based on False Witnesses
Discusses the right to intercourse when a judge rules on false witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a man may have intercourse with a woman when a judge ruled in her favor based on witnesses, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits intercourse based on the judge's ruling; the Sahibayn forbid it because the witnesses are false.

This part of the passage addresses a scenario where a woman claims a man married her, and the judge accepts false witnesses and declares the marriage valid. The scholars differ: Abu Hanifa allows the man to have intercourse because the judge's ruling is based on proof, while the Sahibayn say it is not allowed because the witnesses are liars. We analyze their reasoning and the underlying principles of evidence and judicial authority.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario and the Ruling
A woman claims a man married her, but he denies it. The judge rules in her favor based on witnesses (who are actually liars). The question: can the man have intercourse with her?
The man knows he did not marry her.
2
Identify the Dispute
Abu Hanifa says he has the right to have intercourse. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say he does not.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the Proof for Each Side
Sahibayn argue that the judge erred because the witnesses are liars, so the ruling is void. Abu Hanifa argues that the witnesses are 'truthful' in the eyes of the court (zahir), and it is impossible to verify inner truthfulness, so the ruling stands.
The analogy is made with witnesses who turn out to be slaves or disbelievers; those can be verified easily, so the ruling would be void.
4
Analyze the Basis: Truth vs Appearance
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between cases where the error is easily detectable (slavery, disbelief) and cases where it is not (truthfulness). The judge's ruling based on apparent evidence is enforceable inwardly (batinan) to end disputes.
This is a principle about the finality of judicial rulings.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the man may lawfully have intercourse despite knowing the marriage is false. Under Sahibayn, he must abstain and seek legal remedy.
This affects the permissibility of intercourse in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والموقت وله وطء امرأة ادعت عليه أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها ببينة ولم يكن تزوجها .
معنى
بخلاف المتعة فإنه لو قال «أتمتع بك ولم يذكر مدة كان متعة. والتحقيق ما في فتح القدير أن المتعة عقد على امرأة لا يراد به مقاصد عقد النكاح من القرار للولد وتربيته بل إما إلى مدة معينة ينتهي العقد بانتهائها أو غير معينة بمعنى بقاء العقد ما دام معها إلى أن ينصرف عنها فيدخل فيه بمادة المتعة والنكاح الموقت أيضاً فيكون من أفراد المتعة وإن عقد بلفظ التزويج وأحضر الشهود إلى آخر ما ذكره. وقد نقل في الهداية إجماع الصحابة على حرمته وأنها كانت مباحة ثم نسخت. وفي صحيح مسلم عنه كنت أذنت لكم في الاستمتاع الله ذلك إلى يوم القيامة» (۱) والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة شهيرة، وما نقل عن
بالنساء وقد حرم ابن عباس من إباحتها فقد صح رجوعه وما في الهداية من نسبته إلى مالك فغلط كما ذكره الشارحون، فحينئذ كان زفر القائل بإباحة الموقت محجوجاً بالإجماع لما علمت أن الموقت من أفراد المتعة. قالوا : ثلاثة أشياء نسخت مرتين : المتعة ولحوم الحمر الأهلية والتوجه إلى بيت المقدس. أطلق في الموقت فشمل المدة الطويلة أيضاً كأن يتزوجها إلى مائتي سنة وهو ظاهر المذهب وهو الصحيح كما في المعراج، لأن التأقيت هو المعين لجهة المتعة. وشمل المدة المجهولة أيضاً. وقيد بالموقت لأنه لو تزوجها على أن يطلقها بعد شهر، فإنه جائز لأن اشتراط القاطع يدل على انعقاده مؤبداً وبطل الشرط. كما في القنية. ولو تزوجها وفي نيته أن يقعد معها مدة نواها فالنكاح صحيح لأن التوقيت إنما يكون باللفظ. قالوا: ولا بأس بتزوج النهاريات وهو أن يتزوجها ليقعد معها نهاراً دون الليل. وينبغي أن لا يكون هذا الشرط لازماً عليها ولها أن تطلب المبيت عندها ليلاً لما عرف في باب القسم. قوله: (وله وطء امرأة ادعت أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها مبينة ولم يكن تزوجها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ليس له وطؤها لأن القاضي أخطأ الحجة إذ الشهود كذبة فصار كما إذا ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار. ولأبي حنيفة أن الشهود صدقة عنده وهو الحجة لتعذر الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق بخلاف الكفر والرق لأن الوقوف عليهما متيسر فإذا ابتنى القضاء على الحجة وأمكن تنفيذه باطناً بتقديم النكاح نفذ قطعاً للمنازعة بخلاف الأملاك المرسلة لأن في

And the timed [marriage] - and he has the right to have intercourse with a woman who claimed that he married her and the judge ruled in favor of her marriage based on evidence while he did not marry her. Unlike mut'a, because if he said 'I enjoy being with you' and did not mention a duration, it is mut'a. Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada'): Judicial ruling; the decision of a judge that is binding on the parties.
بينة (bayyinah): Proof, typically two witnesses, required to establish a claim in court.
شهود زور (shuhud zur): False witnesses; those who give false testimony.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced

Inward Effect of a Judge's Ruling Based on False Testimony in Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inward effect of judicial ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the inward effectiveness of a judge's ruling based on false testimony in a marriage case, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the permissibility of intercourse.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective inwardly according to Abu Hanifa, making intercourse permissible; the Sahibayn disagree, holding the ruling invalid inwardly.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. When a judge rules based on false testimony, does that ruling carry force in the sight of Allah (batinan)? Abu Hanifa and his two famous students differ, and this difference has direct consequences for whether the man may have intercourse with the woman. Understanding this dispute requires analyzing the nature of judicial proof (al-hujja) and the limits of outward certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A woman claims a man married her. The judge, based on two false witnesses, rules that the marriage is valid. The man knows the witnesses are lying. The question is: may he have intercourse with her?
The woman is assumed to be legally eligible for marriage (muhallil li al-insha').
2
State the Hanafi Position
Abu Hanifa holds that the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. Therefore, the man may have intercourse, and the woman must allow it. However, the man is sinful for making the false claim (but not for the intercourse itself).
The key principle: al-qada' yunfidh fi al-zahir wa al-batin fi al-'uqood wa al-fusukh.
3
State the Sahibayn's Objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that since the witnesses are liars, the proof (al-hujja) is invalid. The ruling is an error and not effective inwardly. Therefore, intercourse is not permissible; it would be zina.
They analogize to cases where witnesses are revealed to be slaves or disbelievers.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Dalil
Abu Hanifa argues that truthfulness of witnesses cannot be verified externally, unlike slavery or disbelief. The judge's ruling is based on a valid proof (the witnesses), and to end disputes, it must be effective inwardly. He also uses an analogy: a buyer falsely claims rescission of a sale of a slave girl; the judge rules for him; the seller may still have intercourse with her despite knowing the claim is false.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy).
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
The practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, intercourse is halal (though sinful for the false claim); according to the two students, it is haram (zina). The author notes that al-Faqih Abu al-Layth gave fatwa on the students' view, but Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah state that Abu Hanifa's view is more correct.
The dispute also extends to divorce and other contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وله وطء امرأة ادعت أنه تزوجها وقضى بنكاحها مبينة ولم يكن تزوجها وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ليس له وطؤها لأن القاضي أخطأ الحجة إذ الشهود كذبة فصار كما إذا ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار. ولأبي حنيفة أن الشهود صدقة عنده وهو الحجة لتعذر الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق بخلاف الكفر والرق لأن الوقوف عليهما متيسر فإذا ابتنى القضاء على الحجة وأمكن تنفيذه باطناً بتقديم النكاح نفذ قطعاً للمنازعة بخلاف الأملاك المرسلة لأن في
اشتراط الشهود وتعيين المدة وفي الموقت الشهود وتعيين المدة. قال في الفتح : ولا شك أنه لا دليل لهؤلاء على تعيين كون نكاح المتعة الذي أباحه ثـم حـرمـه هـو مـا اجـتـمـع فـيـه مـادة م ت ع للقطع من الآثار بأن المتحقق ليس إلا أنه أذن لهم في المتعة، وليس معنى هذا أن من باشر هذا المأذون فيه يتعين عليه أن يخاطبها بلفظ التمتع ونحوه لما عرف من أن اللفظ إنما يطلق ويراد
معناه، فإذا قال تمتعوا من هذه النسوة فليس مفهومه قولو أتمتع بك بل أوجدوا معنى هذا اللفظ، ومعناه المشهور أن يوجد عقداً على امرأة إلى آخر ما يأتي قوله : (فيدخل فيه ما بمادة المتعة والنكاح الموقت أيضاً) قلت : مما يؤيد هذا التحقيق ما في الخانية : ولو قال تزوجتك شهراً فرضيت عندنا يكون متعة ولا يكون نكاحاً، وقال زفر رحمه الله : يصح النكاح ويبطل الشرط قوله : (وذكر المصنف : الكافي أنه أخذ به عامة المشايخ ذكر المؤلف في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي أنه المعتمد قوله : (مع أنه يمكنه التخلص بالعتق قد يقال إن العتق فرع عن ثبوت الملك فإن كان ثابتاً فلا حاجة إلى العتق وإلا فلا يجديه نفعاً تأمل قوله : ( ولا يخفي إنه لا يلزم الخ) راجع لأصل المسألة لا لما في الفتح.

كتاب النكاح فصل في المحرمات

الأسباب تزاحماً فلا إمكان وهذه المسألة فرد من أفراد المسألة الآتية في " كتاب القضاء وهي أن القضاء ينفذ بشهادة الزور ظاهراً وباطناً في العقود والفسوخ وكما يجوز له وطؤها يجوز لها تمكينه منه. وكذا لو ادعى عليها النكاح فحكمه كذلك، وكذا لو قضى بالطلاق بشهادة الزور مع علمها حل لها التزوج بآخر بعد العدة وحل للشاهد تزوجها وحرمت على الأول. وعند أبي يوسف : لا تحل للأول ولا للثاني وعند محمد تحل للأول ما لم يدخل بها الثاني، فإذا دخل بها حرمت عليه لوجوب العدة كالمنكوحة. إذا وطئت بشبهة . وأشار بقوله وقضى بنكاحها إلى اشتراط أن تكون محللاً للإنشاء حتى لو كانت ذات زوج أو في عدة غيره أو مطلقه منه ثلاثاً لا ينفذ قضاؤه لأنه لا يقدر على الإنشاء في هذه الحالة. واختلفوا في اشتراط حضور الشهود عند قوله «قضيت فشرطه جماعة للنفاد باطناً عنده، وذكر المصنف في الكافي أنه أخذ به عامة المشايخ، وقيل لا يشترط لأن العقد ثبت مقتضى صحة قضائه في الباطن وما ثبت مقتضى صحة الغير لا يثبت بشرائطه كالبيع في قوله أعتق عبدك عني بألف». وذكر في فتح القدير أن الأوجه عدم الاشتراط ويدل عليه إطلاق المتون. وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث أن الفتوى على قولهما في أصل المسألة أعني عدم النفاذ باطناً فيما ذكر. وفي فتح القدير والنهاية : وقول أبي حنيفة أوجه، وقد استدل له بدلالة الإجماع على أن من اشترى جارية ثم ادعى فسخ بيعها كذباً وبرهن فقضى به حل للبائع وطؤها واستخدامها مع علمه بكذب دعوى المشتري مع أنه يمكنه التخلص بالعتق وإن كان فيه إتلاف ماله فإنه ابتلي بأمرين فعليه أن يختار أهونهما وذلك ما يسلم له فيه دينه ا هـ . ولا يخفى أنه لا يلزم من القول بحل الوطء عدم إثمه فإنه أثم بسبب إقدامه على الدعوى الباطلة وإن كان لا إثم عليه بسبب الوطء، والحق في الهداية بالعقود والفسوخ العتق والنسب، وقد وقعت لطيفة هي أن بعض المغاربة بحث مع الأكمل بأنه يمكن قطع المنازعة بالطلاق فأجابه الأكمل ما تريد بالطلاق الطلاق المشروع أو غيره لا عبرة بغيره والمشروع يستلزم المطلوب إذ لا يتحقق إلا في نكاح صحيح وتعقبه تلميذه عمر قارئ الهداية بأنه جواب غير صحيح لأن له أن يريد غير المشروع ليكون طريقاً إلى قطع المنازعة وإن لم يكن في نفسه صحيحاً. وتعقبهما تلميذه ابن الهمام بأن الحق
معناه، فإذا قال تمتعوا من هذه النسوة فليس مفهومه قولو أتمتع بك بل أوجدوا معنى هذا اللفظ، ومعناه المشهور أن يوجد عقداً على امرأة إلى آخر ما يأتي قوله : (فيدخل فيه ما بمادة المتعة والنكاح الموقت أيضاً) قلت : مما يؤيد هذا التحقيق ما في الخانية : ولو قال تزوجتك شهراً فرضيت عندنا يكون متعة ولا يكون نكاحاً، وقال زفر رحمه الله : يصح النكاح ويبطل الشرط قوله : (وذكر المصنف : الكافي أنه أخذ به عامة المشايخ ذكر المؤلف في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي أنه المعتمد قوله : (مع أنه يمكنه التخلص بالعتق قد يقال إن العتق فرع عن ثبوت الملك فإن كان ثابتاً فلا حاجة إلى العتق وإلا فلا يجديه نفعاً تأمل قوله : ( ولا يخفي إنه لا يلزم الخ) راجع لأصل المسألة لا لما في الفتح.
His statement: 'And he has the right to have intercourse with a woman who claimed that he married her and the judge ruled in favor of her marriage with evidence while he did not marry her' — this is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does not have the right to have intercourse with her because the judge made an error in the proof, since the witnesses are liars, so it is like when they appear to be slaves or disbelievers. For Abu Hanifa, the witnesses are truthful according to him, and they are the proof, because it is impossible to ascertain the reality of truthfulness, unlike disbelief and slavery because ascertaining them is easy. So when the ruling is based on proof and it is possible to execute it inwardly by assuming the marriage, it executes definitively to end the dispute, unlike absolute possessions because in... stipulation of witnesses and specifying the duration, and in timed marriage, witnesses and specifying the duration. He said in al-Fath: There is no doubt that there is no evidence for these people to specify that the mut'a marriage which was permitted then forbidden is that which combines the root m-t-' (mut'a) based on the definitive transmission that what is verified is only that he permitted them temporary enjoyment, and this does not mean that the one who engages in this permitted act must address her with the wording of 'tamattu'' or the like, because it is known that the wording is only used and intended for its meaning. So if he said 'Enjoy these women,' its understanding is not 'Say I enjoy you,' but rather create the meaning of this wording. Its well-known meaning is that a contract with a woman exists, up to his statement: 'So it includes what is of the root of mut'a and also the timed marriage.' I say: Supporting this verification is what is in al-Khaniyah: 'If one said, 'I marry you for a month' and she agreed, in our view it is mut'a and not marriage, and Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The marriage is valid and the condition is void.' His statement: 'And the author mentioned in al-Kafi that the general body of scholars adopted it' — the author mentioned in the book 'The Judge to the Judge' that it is relied upon. His statement: 'Although he can exit through manumission' — it may be said that manumission is a branch of establishing ownership; if it is established, there is no need for manumission, otherwise it is of no benefit. Consider. His statement: 'And it is not hidden that it does not necessitate...' refers back to the original issue, not to what is in al-Fath. In the chapter of Nikah, section on prohibited women, page 191: The causes are numerous so there is no possibility. And this issue is a branch of the upcoming issue in the Book of Judiciary: that a ruling based on false witnesses is effective outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions. And just as it is permissible for him to have intercourse with her, it is permissible for her to allow him. Similarly, if he claims marriage against her, the same ruling applies. Similarly, if the judge rules a divorce based on false witnesses with her knowledge, it becomes permissible for her to marry another after the waiting period, and permissible for the witness to marry her, and she becomes forbidden to the first husband. According to Abu Yusuf: She is not permissible to the first nor the second. According to Muhammad: She is permissible to the first as long as the second has not had intercourse with her; when the second has intercourse with her, she becomes forbidden to the first due to the obligation of the waiting period, like a woman who is married after intercourse under ambiguity. And he indicated by his statement 'and the judge ruled in favor of her marriage' the condition that she must be legally capable of contracting a marriage; so if she was married to another, or in the waiting period of another, or his thrice-divorced wife, his ruling is not effective because he cannot contract a marriage in that state. They differed regarding the condition of the presence of witnesses when he says 'I have ruled' — a group stipulates it for inward effectiveness according to him, and the author mentioned in al-Kafi that the general body of scholars adopted it, and it is said it is not stipulated because the contract is established based on the validity of his ruling inwardly, and what is established based on the validity of another is not established by its conditions, like the sale in his statement 'Free your slave from me for a thousand.' It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that the correct view is not to stipulate, and the general wording of the texts indicates it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that the fatwa is according to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view in the original issue, i.e., the absence of inward effectiveness in what was mentioned. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah: Abu Hanifa's view is more correct, and he supported it by the indication of consensus that if someone buys a slave girl, then falsely claims the repudiation of her sale and provides evidence, and the judge rules accordingly, it is permissible for the seller to have intercourse with her and use her despite knowing the falsity of the buyer's claim, even though he could free her to escape, although that would involve destroying his wealth. He is faced with two matters; he must choose the lesser of two evils and that which preserves his religion. It is not hidden that the ruling that intercourse is permissible does not negate his sin — he is sinful because of his false claim, even if he is not sinful due to the intercourse. The truth in al-Hidayah is regarding contracts and dissolutions, manumission and lineage. A subtle point occurred: a Maghribi scholar debated with al-Akmal saying that the dispute can be ended by divorce. Al-Akmal replied: 'What do you mean by divorce — the legislated divorce or other? Other is not considered; the legislated entails the desired, as it can only occur in a valid marriage.' His student Umar Qari' al-Hidayah criticized that this answer is incorrect because he could intend non-legislated divorce as a means to end the dispute, even if not valid in itself. His student Ibn al-Humann criticized both, saying the truth is... its meaning. So if he said 'Enjoy these women,' its understanding is not 'Say I enjoy you,' but rather create the meaning of this wording. Its well-known meaning is that a contract with a woman exists, up to his statement: 'So it includes what is of the root of mut'a and also the timed marriage.' I say: Supporting this verification is what is in al-Khaniyah: 'If one said, 'I marry you for a month' and she agreed, in our view it is mut'a and not marriage, and Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The marriage is valid and the condition is void.' His statement: 'And the author mentioned in al-Kafi that the general body of scholars adopted it' — the author mentioned in the book 'The Judge to the Judge' that it is relied upon. His statement: 'Although he can exit through manumission' — it may be said that manumission is a branch of establishing ownership; if it is established, there is no need for manumission, otherwise it is of no benefit. Consider. His statement: 'And it is not hidden that it does not necessitate...' refers back to the original issue, not to what is in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a scenario where a woman claims a man married her, but the man knows it is false. The judge rules in her favor based on testimony from two witnesses whom the man knows are lying. The question is whether the man may have sexual intercourse with her, and whether the ruling is effective inwardly (in the sight of Allah). Abu Hanifa holds that the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly because the judge's proof (the witnesses) is valid externally, and we cannot know the inner truth. Therefore, the man may have intercourse, and the woman must permit him. This is a branch of a broader principle in the Book of Judiciary that a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective in contracts and dissolutions. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, saying that since the man knows the witnesses are false, the ruling is not effective inwardly; thus he cannot have intercourse. The author then discusses further details: similar rulings for divorce, and further differences between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in a divorce scenario. There is also a discussion on whether witnesses must be present at the pronouncement of the ruling for inward effectiveness; the preferred view is that they are not required. The author cites that the fatwa is according to the two students' view on the original issue, but later scholarship (Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihayah) favors Abu Hanifa's view as more correct, using the analogy of a buyer who falsely claims rescission of a sale. Even though the man is sinful for making the false claim, the intercourse itself is not sinful because of the ruling.

Key Terms
القضاء بشهادة الزور (al-qada' bi-shahadat al-zur): A judge's ruling based on false testimony, which according to Abu Hanifa is effective both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions.
النفاذ باطناً (al-nafadh batinan): The ruling being valid in the sight of Allah and in the inner reality, not just outwardly.
المحلل للإنشاء (al-muhallil li al-insha'): A woman legally eligible to contract a new marriage; if she is already married or in waiting period, the judge's ruling is ineffective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the judge's ruling based on false testimony effective inwardly?
A) Because the judge is infallible.
B) Because the witnesses are presumed truthful since their falsehood cannot be externally verified.
C) Because the man consented to the marriage.
D) Because the woman forced the case.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective inwardly according to Abu Hanifa, making intercourse permissible despite the man's knowledge of falsehood, though he bears sin for the false claim.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Hukm al-Qada' bi Shahadat al-Zur 'ala al-Wat'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inward effect of judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the inward effect of a judge's ruling based on false testimony on the permissibility of intercourse, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on false testimony makes intercourse permissible for the defendant, despite the witness's sin.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the extent of a judge's ruling based on false testimony. The Hanafi school generally holds that such a ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions. However, the three eponymous imams diverge on whether this inward effect extends to making intercourse permissible when the ruling concerns marriage. The practical consequences—for the woman, the defendant, and the false witness—depend on which position is adopted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general Hanafi principle
The passage builds on the rule from the Book of Judges: a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective 'outwardly and inwardly' in contracts and dissolutions. This means that even if all parties know the testimony is false, the legal consequences follow in reality (inwardly), not just in appearance.
This principle contrasts with some other schools that may limit inward effect.
2
Apply the principle to the marriage case
The specific case: a judge rules that a woman is married to a man based on false testimony. According to Abu Hanifa, this ruling makes intercourse permissible for the man, and the woman must allow him. The false witness is sinful, but the defendant is not.
The woman's knowledge of the false testimony does not prevent the permissibility.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's positions
Abu Yusuf holds that the woman becomes forbidden to both the first husband (the defendant) and the second (the false witness). Muhammad holds that she remains permissible to the first unless the second consummates, after which she becomes forbidden due to the waiting period.
The Sahibayn limit inward effect in this scenario.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the woman can stay with the first husband; under Abu Yusuf, she must leave both; under Muhammad, she can stay with the first unless the second consummates.
This affects her future marriage options and the validity of any prior ties.

The causes are conflicting so it is not possible. This case is one of the cases of the upcoming issue in the Book of Judges, which is that judgment is executed by false testimony outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions. Just as it is permissible for him to have intercourse with her, it is permissible for her to allow him. Likewise, if he claimed marriage against her, the ruling is the same. Likewise, if he ruled for divorce by false testimony while she knows, it becomes permissible for her to marry another after the waiting period, and it becomes permissible for the witness to marry her, and she becomes forbidden to the first husband. According to Abu Yusuf: she is not permissible to the first nor the second. According to Muhammad: she is permissible to the first as long as the second has not consummated with her; if he consummated, she becomes forbidden to him due to the necessity of the waiting period, like a woman who is married if she is penetrated by mistake. He indicated by his saying 'and he ruled for her marriage' the condition that she be legally capable of initiating marriage; even if she has a husband or is in the waiting period of another or is thrice-divorced from him, his ruling is not executed because he cannot initiate in this situation. They differed regarding the condition of the presence of witnesses at his saying 'I have judged'; a group required it for inward execution according to him (Abu Hanifa). The author mentioned in al-Kafi that the majority of scholars adopted it. It was said it is not required because the contract is established by the requirement of the validity of his judgment inwardly, and what is established by the requirement of the validity of another is not established by its conditions, like the sale in his saying 'Free your slave from me for a thousand'. It was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that the most likely view is that it is not a condition, and the unrestrictedness of the texts supports it. Other is not considered, and legitimate entails the desired, as it cannot occur except in a valid marriage. His student Umar Qari' al-Hidayah criticized this as an incorrect answer, because he can intend non-legitimate as a way to end the dispute even if it is not valid in itself. His student Ibn al-Humam criticized both, saying the truth is its meaning: when he says 'Enjoy yourselves from these women', its understood meaning is not 'I enjoy you' but rather they should create the meaning of this word. His statement: (even though he can free her to avoid sin) it may be said that freeing is a branch of ownership: if ownership is established, there is no need for freeing; otherwise, freeing does not benefit him. Ponder his statement: (and it is not hidden that it does not necessitate...) is referring to the original issue, not to what is in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of a judge's ruling based on false testimony regarding marriage and intercourse. The issue arises from a broader principle in the Book of Judges: that a judge's ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly even if based on false testimony, in contracts and dissolutions. The specific case here is when a judge rules that a woman is married to a man based on false testimony. According to Abu Hanifa, this makes intercourse permissible for the man and the woman must allow him, despite her knowledge that the testimony was false. Abu Yusuf holds that she becomes permissible to neither the first nor the second husband (the witness who testified falsely). Muhammad holds that she remains permissible to the first husband unless the second has consummated, in which case she becomes forbidden due to a waiting period. The passage also discusses conditions for the ruling to be effective inwardly, such as the woman being legally eligible for marriage (not already married, in iddah, or thrice-divorced from the same man). There is disagreement about whether the presence of witnesses at the judge's pronouncement is required for inward effectiveness; Abu Hanifa's view, as adopted by most scholars according to al-Kafi, is that it is required, but Fath al-Qadir considers the stronger view to be that it is not required. A proof for Abu Hanifa is drawn from analogy with a case where a judge rules on a false claim of rescission of a slave sale: the seller may have intercourse with the slave girl even though he knows the claim is false. The passage concludes with a discussion about whether divorce could serve as an alternative to the judge's ruling, with the response that only legitimate divorce matters, but that the possibility of non-legitimate divorce is not considered effective. A final point clarifies that the permissibility of intercourse does not negate the sin of the false witness, who is sinful for his false claim.

Key Terms
قضاء بشهادة الزور (qada' bi shahadat al-zur): A judge's ruling based on testimony that is known to be false by all parties.
النفاذ باطناً (al-nafadh batinan): The ruling being legally effective in reality, not just in appearance, so that the resulting actions are permissible in the sight of Allah.
محللاً للإنشاء (muhallal lil-insha'): Legally capable of entering into a new marriage contract, i.e., not already married, in iddah, or thrice-divorced from the same man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the effect of a judge's ruling based on false testimony that a woman is married to a man?
A) The woman becomes permissible to the first husband only if the second does not consummate.
B) The woman becomes permissible to the first husband, and he may have intercourse with her, though the witness is sinful.
C) The woman becomes permissible to neither the first nor the second husband.
D) The ruling has no effect inwardly, only outwardly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally holds that a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective inwardly, but the three imams differ on whether this extends to making intercourse permissible; the practical consequences vary, and later authorities differ on the tarjih.

Guardian (Wali) in Marriage: Hanafi Ruling and Definition
Definition of wali and ruling on marriage without guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the role of a guardian in the marriage of a free mature woman and explain the legal definition of wali.

Core Idea
A free mature woman's marriage is valid without a guardian — she acts in her exclusive right.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes the foundational Hanafi position that a free, mature woman does not require a guardian for a valid marriage. It then expands on the definition of 'wali' from linguistic, legal, and theological perspectives, distinguishing between recommendatory and compulsory guardianship. You will learn to apply these distinctions in evaluating marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the statement 'نفذ نكاح حرة مكلفة بلا ولي' in the matn. This is the school's definitive position that a guardian is not required for a free mature woman's marriage.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Analyse the definition of wali
Break down the legal definition: 'البالغ العاقل الوارث' (mature, sane, inheritor). Identify the categories excluded: minors, insane, and non-Muslims. Note the hashya objection about 'inheritor'.
The hashya from al-Ramli argues that the judge is a guardian but not an inheritor.
3
Distinguish the two types of wilayat
Explain wilayat nadb (recommendatory) over mature women, and wilayat ijbar (compulsory) over minors, insane, and slaves. Note the consequence: a mature woman is not compelled.
This distinction is critical for understanding who can contract marriage.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Given a case of a 25-year-old free Muslim woman who contracts her own marriage without a guardian, state the ruling: the marriage is sahih and binding.
Compare with Shafi'i school which requires a guardian.

Chapter of Guardians and Competent Matches. The marriage of a free, mature woman is executed without a guardian, and a mature virgin is not compelled into marriage; if the guardian seeks her permission... A beginning in explaining what is not a condition for the validity of marriage according to us, i.e., the guardian. It has a linguistic, legal, and theological meaning. Linguistically, al-wali is the opposite of enemy; al-wilayah (with kasr) is authority, and al-wilayah (with fatha) is help. Sibawayh said: al-wilayah with fatha is the infinitive, and with kasr is the noun like imarah and niqabah, because it is a name for what you undertake and carry out. When they intend the infinitive, they use fatha, as in al-Sihah. Legally, it is the mature, sane, inheritor. Thus excluded are the minor, the insane, and the disbeliever over a Muslim woman. In the principles of religion, it is the one who knows Allah Almighty and His names and attributes to the extent possible, who is constant in acts of obedience, avoids sins, and is not immersed in desires and pleasures, as in Sharh al-Aqa'id. Wilayah in fiqh is the execution of a statement over another whether they like it or not. In marriage, it is of two types: wilayat nadb (recommendation) and istihbab (preference), which is the guardianship over a sane, mature woman, whether virgin or non-virgin; and wilayat ijbar (compulsion), which is guardianship over a minor, whether virgin or non-virgin, and similarly over a mature insane woman and a slave woman. Guardianship is established by four causes: kinship, ownership, clientage, and imamate. The plural of kuf' is akfa', meaning the equivalent, as in al-Mughrib; its explanation will come later. Its people. His statement: 'The marriage of a free, mature woman is executed without a guardian' because she acts in her exclusive right and she is among those capable of action. And 'al-akfa': His statement: (thus the author explicitly stated etc.) said in al-Ramz: I say, in its explanation there is a sound way, which is that divorce is linked to the obligation of dower; so if they testify against him for a large dower and most or all of it is tied to divorce, because she desires to stay with him, he has a strong deterrent from divorce, especially if he is very poor. The summary is that divorce may not be a way to end the dispute even if she is the plaintiff. Chapter of Guardians and Competent Matches. His statement: (and legally it is the mature, sane, inheritor) al-Ramli objected that mentioning inheritor is not appropriate because the judge is a guardian but not an inheritor.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on guardians and competent matches (باب الأولياء والأكفاء) from Kanz al-Daqaiq, a Hanafi matn. The core ruling is stated in the matn: 'The marriage of a free, mature woman is valid without a guardian.' This establishes that in the Hanafi school, a guardian is not a condition for the validity of the marriage contract for a free woman who has reached maturity and is sane. The commentary then provides a detailed definition of the term 'wali' from three perspectives: linguistic, legal (fiqhi), and theological (usuli). Linguistically, wali is the opposite of enemy, and wilayah (authority) is distinguished from wilayyah (help). Sibawayh explains the difference between the fatha and kasr vowels. Legally, the wali is defined as a mature, sane, inheritor, thus excluding minors, the insane, and non-Muslims from being guardians over a Muslim woman. Theologically, wali is a saintly person. The passage then explains the two types of wilayah in marriage: wilayat al-nadb (recommendatory guardianship) over a sane mature woman (she is not compelled but may seek advice), and wilayat al-ijbar (compulsory guardianship) over minors, insane women, and slaves. Guardianship is established by four causes: kinship, ownership, clientage, and imamate. The commentary also includes a hashya from al-Ramli objecting to the inclusion of 'inheritor' in the legal definition, as a judge is a guardian but not necessarily an inheritor. The final part of the passage includes a marginal note about divorce that might belong to the previous lesson.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): In fiqh: the mature, sane, inheritor who has authority over a woman in marriage. In this passage, it is defined legally as such, with the hashya objecting to the inclusion of 'inheritor'.
ولاية ندب (wilayat nadb): Guardianship of recommendation: the guardian's role is advisory and recommended for a mature, sane woman; she is not compelled.
ولاية إجبار (wilayat ijbar): Guardianship of compulsion: the guardian can compel the marriage of a minor, insane woman, or slave woman without her consent.
كفء (kuf'): Competent match; equivalent in status, lineage, religion, etc. The plural is akfa'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, the marriage of a free, mature woman without a guardian is:
A) Invalid
B) Valid and binding
C) Valid but requires subsequent approval
D) Suspended until guardian agrees

Key Takeaway
A free mature woman's marriage is valid without a guardian because she has full legal capacity in her exclusive right.

Marriage of a Free Adult Woman Without a Guardian
Establishes the validity of a free adult woman's marriage without a guardian with Quranic and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a free adult woman's marriage without a guardian, explain the primary Quranic and Hadith proofs, and evaluate the counter-arguments from other schools.

Core Idea
A free adult woman can validly marry without a guardian – she is the master of her own marriage contract.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a cornerstone of Hanafi nikah jurisprudence: the validity of a free adult woman's self-conducted marriage. While the Shafi'i school insists on a guardian's presence, the Hanafi school grounds its position in clear Quranic attribution of the marriage act to the woman herself and an authentic prophetic hadith. In this lesson, you will trace the Hanafi proofs and understand how they rebut opposing evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine what exactly is being ruled: the marriage of a free, adult, sane woman (hurrah mukallafah) without a guardian. Note that the ruling is that it is executed (nafadha).
The passage explicitly states 'نفذ نكاح حرة مكلفة بلا ولي' – it is valid and operative.
2
Examine the rationale and underlying principle
The text argues that she acts in her pure right (khalis haqqiha) and is capable like she is with property. The general principle: whoever can manage their wealth can marry themselves.
This analogizes marriage to property management, a key Hanafi method.
3
Analyze the primary evidences
Focus on Quran 2:230 'until she marries' (attributing the act to her) and the hadith 'al-aym ahaqqu bi nafsiha' (the unmarried woman has more right to herself). Understand how they prove her capacity.
The Quranic verb 'tankiha' is feminine, indicating the woman is the agent.
4
Evaluate the opposing hadiths and the Hanafi response
The text addresses hadiths that seemingly require a guardian. It declares them weak or interprets them as applying to slaves, minors, or as indicating perfection, not necessity.
This shows the Hanafi method of tawil and al-jarh wa al-ta'dil.
5
Note the exception: guardian's objection for incompatibility
While the marriage is valid even without a guardian, the guardian retains the right to object if the husband is not kuf' (compatible). This does not affect the contract's initial validity.
The last line: 'لكن للولي الاعتراض في غير الكفء' – but the guardian may object in case of non-kuf'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفذ نكاح حرة مكلفة بلا ولي لأنها تصرفت في خالص حقها وهي من أهل التصرف لكونها عاقلة بالغة، ولهذا كان لها التصرف في المال ولها اختيار الأزواج. وإنما يطالب الولي بالتزويج كيلا تنسب إلى الوقاحة، ولذا كان المستحب في حقها تفويض الأمر إليه. والأصل هنا أن كل من يجوز تصرفه في ماله بولاية نفسه يجوز نكاحه على نفسه، وكل من لا يجوز تصرفه في ماله بولاية نفسه لا يجوز نكاحه على نفسه ويدل عليه قوله تعالى حتى تنكح [البقرة: ۲۳۰] أضاف النكاح إليها. ومن السنة حديث مسلم «الأيم أحق بنفسها من وليها»(١) وهي من لا زوج لها بكراً كانت أو ثيباً. فأفاد أن فيه حقين: حقه وهو مباشرته عقد النكاح برضاها وقد جعلها أحق منه ولن تكون أحق إلا إذا زوجت نفسها بغير رضاه، وأما ما رواه الترمذي وحسنه أيما امرأة نكحت بغير إذن وليها فنكاحها باطل»(٢) وما رواه أبو داود «لا نكاح إلا بولي» (۳) فضعيفان أو مختلف في صحتهما فلن يعارضا المتفق على أو الأول محمول على الأمة والصغيرة والمعتوهة أو على غير الكفء، والثاني محمول على نفي الكمال، أو هي ولية نفسها وفائدته نفي نكاح من لا ولاية له كالكافر للمسلمة والمعتوهة والأمة، كل ذلك لدفع التعارض مع أن الحديث الأول حجة على من لم يعتبر عبارة النساء في النكاح فإن مفهومه أنها إذا نكحت بإذن وليها فنكاحها صحيح وهم لا يقولون به . وأما قوله تعالى ولا تعضلوهن أن ينكحن أزواجهن ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۲] فالمراد بالعضل المنع حساً بأن يحبسها في بيت ويمنعها من أن تتزوج كما في المبسوط إن كان نهياً للأولياء لا المنع العقد بدليل أن ينكحن حيث أضاف العقد إليهن وإن كان نهياً للأزواج المطلقين عن المنع عن التزوج بعد العدة كما في المعراج بدليل أنه قال في أول الآية وإذا طلقتم النساء [البقرة : ٢٣٢] فلم يكن حجة أصلاً قيده بالحرة احترازاً عن الأمة والمكاتبة وأم الولد فإنه لا يجوز نكاحهن إلا بإذن المولى. وقيده بالمكلفة احترازاً عن الصغيرة والمجنونة فإنه لا ينعقد نكاحهما إلا بالولي وأطلقها فشمل البكر والثيب، وأطلق فشمل الكفء وغيره. وهذا ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه لكن للولي الاعتراض في غير الكفء.
The marriage of a free, legally responsible woman is executed without a guardian because she acted in her pure right and she is capable of acting, being sane and adult. Therefore, she has authority over her wealth and choice of spouses. The guardian is only asked to marry her to avoid her being attributed with shamelessness, so it is recommended for her to delegate the matter to him. The principle here is that whoever is allowed to act in his wealth by his own authority, his marriage is valid on himself, and whoever is not allowed to act in his wealth by his own authority, his marriage is not valid on himself. This is evidenced by His statement 'until she marries' [Al-Baqarah 2:230] – He attributed the marriage to her. And from the Sunnah is the hadith of Muslim: 'The one without a husband has more right to herself than her guardian' – she is one without a husband, whether virgin or non-virgin. This indicates that there are two rights: his right, which is to directly conduct the marriage contract with her consent, but she has been made more entitled, and she would only be more entitled if she marries herself without his consent. As for what al-Tirmidhi narrated and considered good: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid,' and what Abu Dawud narrated: 'No marriage except with a guardian,' they are weak or disputed in their authenticity, so they do not contradict what is agreed upon. Or the first is interpreted as referring to the slave girl, the minor, the insane, or to one who is not a compatible match, and the second is interpreted as negation of perfection, or she is her own guardian, and its benefit is negation of the marriage of one who has no guardianship, such as a Muslim woman marrying a non-Muslim, an insane person, or a slave – all this to avoid contradiction. Moreover, the first hadith is evidence against those who do not consider women's statements in marriage, because its implication is that if she marries with her guardian's permission, her marriage is valid, and they do not say that. As for His statement 'And do not prevent them from marrying their husbands' [Al-Baqarah 2:232], the intended meaning of prevention is physical prevention by imprisoning her in a house and preventing her from marrying, as in al-Mabsut, if it is a prohibition for guardians, not prevention of the contract, evidenced by 'that they marry' where the contract is attributed to them. If it is a prohibition for the divorcing husbands from preventing marriage after the waiting period, as in al-Mi'raj, evidenced by His saying at the beginning of the verse 'And when you divorce women' [Al-Baqarah 2:232], so it was not a proof at all. He restricted it to 'free woman' to exclude the slave girl, the mudabbara, the mukataba, and the umm walad, for their marriage is not valid without the master's permission. And he restricted it to 'legally responsible' to exclude the minor and the insane, for their marriage is not contracted except with a guardian. He made it absolute, so it includes virgin and non-virgin, and absolute, so it includes a compatible match and others. This is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa and his two companions, but the guardian has the right to object in the case of an incompatible match.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof type. It begins by stating the Hanafi position that the marriage of a free, sane, adult woman is valid without a guardian. The commentator then provides the rationale: she is acting in her own right and is capable of managing her own affairs, just as she can manage her wealth. The guardian's involvement is only recommended (mustahabb) to avoid impropriety. The passage then establishes a general principle: whoever can independently manage his own wealth can marry himself. This is supported by two primary proofs: (1) The Quranic verse 'until she marries' (al-Baqarah 2:230), which attributes the act of marriage to the woman herself, indicating her capacity to contract it. (2) The authentic hadith from Muslim: 'The unmarried woman has more right to herself than her guardian.' This hadith shows that the woman has a superior right to marry herself, implying that her marriage without the guardian's consent is valid. The passage then rebuts opposing hadiths (from al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud) by declaring them weak or subject to interpretation. The first is explained as referring to slaves, minors, or incompatible matches; the second is interpreted as indicating perfection or ruling out specific cases like a Muslim woman marrying a non-Muslim. The verse on 'adl' (al-Baqarah 2:232) is also clarified: it forbids physical impediment, not the act of contracting. Finally, the commentary explains the qualifications in the original statement: 'free' excludes slaves, 'legally responsible' excludes minors and the insane. It also notes that while the ruling is absolute regarding compatibility, the guardian has a right to object if the match is not suitable (kuf').

Key Terms
حرة (hurrah): A free woman, as opposed to a slave, mudabbara, mukataba, or umm walad
مكلفة (mukallafah): A sane, adult woman legally responsible (baaligha, aaqila)
ولي (wali): Guardian; in fiqh: a sane adult male who is an heir (or ruler).
كفء (kuf'): Compatibility in marriage; social, religious, and economic suitability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Quran 2:232
B) Hadith 'al-aym ahaqqu bi nafsiha' (the unmarried woman has more right to herself)
C) Hadith 'no marriage without a guardian'
D) Consensus (ijma)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a free adult woman can validly conduct her own marriage without a guardian, relying on Quran 2:230 and the authentic hadith giving her superior right.

Nikah — Marriage
